<span id="freeTextContainer6713994328979709414">okay. when i read <i>‘daughter of smoke and bone,’</i> i complained that the relationship felt too insta-lovey. and now after reading this, im going to complain that there wasnt enough love. WHO EVEN AM I?! i just really want to see karou and akiva happy and heathy and in love. is that too much to ask!? <br/><br/>overall, this wasnt bad! ive seen nothing but absolute obsession when it comes to this series, and i desperately wanted to feel the same. after ADOSAB, i thought i was on the right track, but after read</span>
  <span id="freeText6713994328979709414" style="display:none">okay. when i read <i>‘daughter of smoke and bone,’</i> i complained that the relationship felt too insta-lovey. and now after reading this, im going to complain that there wasnt enough love. WHO EVEN AM I?! i just really want to see karou and akiva happy and heathy and in love. is that too much to ask!? <br /><br />overall, this wasnt bad! ive seen nothing but absolute obsession when it comes to this series, and i desperately wanted to feel the same. after ADOSAB, i thought i was on the right track, but after reading this, maybe the whole monsters vs. angels just really isnt my thing? the story was definitely entertaining enough (even though this was a classic second book series filler), but there is just something missing for me to fall in head over heels in love with this story. <br /><br />i will admit that the writing was lovely. there were times when the language felt like pure poetry, with some sentences being quite moving. you can really see how laini taylor has developed her style from one book to the next. and even though not much happened in this, i do think the series is headed in a good direction overall and i will most likely be picking up the next book! so fingers crossed!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>

  <span id="freeText17336919436530557818" style="display:none">Only one word can describe my feelings about this book:<br><br>Fuck. <br><br><i>Fuck. <br><br><b>FUCK</b></i>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1405342364ra/10384068.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Don’t take that the wrong way. I mean it in a good way. <i>A very good way</i>. <br><br>You know why I love this series so much? Because it’s different. I’d previously rage-quit reading anything even remotely YA because I just can’t with the contrived drama, and the angst, and the dopey, sappy, first time love, and the Mary Sues. The goddamn Mary Sues. <br><br>Authors, stahp it with the goddamn Mary Sues. <br><br>And then there’s the love triangles. Anyone who’s spoken to me for a fraction of a second on here probably already knows exactly how I feel about love triangles because I carry a banner with me from thread to thread that announces my feelings on that subject. Its message is aided by the fifty megaphones I keep strapped to my person, the volume set to stun as they blare forth:<br><br><b>
  <i>“AUTHORS, STAHP IT WITH THE MOTHER FUCKING LOVE TRIANGLES.”</i>
</b><br><br>But then there’s YA born from the brain of Laini Taylor. I’ll read it. Nay, I’ll devour it. Breathe it in and hold it in my lungs for as long as possible before I’m forced to exhale or lose consciousness. I’m not saying that she’s exempt from using some of the above themes and tropes. Hell, I think this book has <i>all</i> of them. You know what makes it so different? It’s the beautiful writing, the pacing of the story, the incredible characterization, the depth to which she delves, the entire execution really. <br><br>Unlike so many others in this category, she makes these overused themes believable, relatable, and addicting as fuck. Therefore, she gets ALL THE STARS.<br><br><b><a href="http://www.thealliterates.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thealliterates" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/the_alliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></b></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_311177914" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/311177914" />
    <a title="Keertana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana"><img alt="Keertana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438801223p2/7584700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/311177914?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=beautiful-prose">beautiful-prose</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer311177914" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6289995636303671146">If <i>Daughter of Smoke and Bone</i> was a dream, a mirage, a masterpiece of writing and phrases and words, overlapped and edited and fine-tuned to create a perfection of romance, snark, and pulsating chemistry, all tinged with a palpable undertone of bittersweet, <i>Days of Blood and Starlight</i> is like a hard slap, the cold splash of water, and the startled opening of ones eyes into the bleak, war-ridden, fragile, and bloody reality of life. Unlike most trilogies which follow in a steady rhythm of romance</span>
  <span id="freeText6289995636303671146" style="display:none">If <i>Daughter of Smoke and Bone</i> was a dream, a mirage, a masterpiece of writing and phrases and words, overlapped and edited and fine-tuned to create a perfection of romance, snark, and pulsating chemistry, all tinged with a palpable undertone of bittersweet, <i>Days of Blood and Starlight</i> is like a hard slap, the cold splash of water, and the startled opening of ones eyes into the bleak, war-ridden, fragile, and bloody reality of life. Unlike most trilogies which follow in a steady rhythm of romance or action or paranormal mystery, Laini Taylor breaks all imaginary constraints and reveals to us the completely unexpected, for <i>Days of Blood and Starlight</i> is as far removed from its predecessor, <i>Daughter of Smoke and Bone,</i> as any novel could possibly be. In fact, the only similarities between the two lie in Taylor's atmospheric writing, her distinct characterizations, and the general plot continuation. In all other aspects though, Laini Taylor has surpassed my wildest expectations and written a novel that I can claim, in full confidence, that is far, <i>far</i> better than its predecessor. I gave <i>Daughter of Smoke and Bone</i> 5 Stars, just as I did <i>Days of Blood and Starlight,</i> but in reality, this novel deserves 500 Stars. <br /><br /><i>Days of Blood and Starlight</i> picks up not long after <i>Daughter of Smoke and Bone</i> ended with Karou coming to the realization that the only family she's ever known has been murdered by the only man she's ever loved. Thus, the tone for <i>Days of Blood and Starlight</i> is set; one of revenge, grief, heartbreak, sorrow, despair, and yet, despite all that, hope. What stands out the most, to me at least, is how <i>real</i> Taylor's novel is. Both <i>Daughter of Smoke and Bone</i> and <i>Days of Blood and Starlight</i> unfold in a sequence of events driven by fate, by destiny, and not entirely by choice, much like our own lives. While we all do have a certain amount of say in the direction our lives lead us, it is only by fate that we meet the people who will change us or affect us in different ways and no one can deny that, at the end of the day, despite all the scattered events throughout our lives, everything comes together and makes a certain degree of sense. <i>Things happen for a reason.</i> For me, <i>Days of Blood and Starlight</i> seemed to echo that very same idea. All the events in Karou's life, first as Madrigal and later as Karou, were leading her up to this point. In fact, nothing could have progressed in this manner if Madrigal had not fallen in love with Akiva, if she had not been beheaded by the Wolf, and later if Akiva had not destroyed Loramendi, the home of the chimeras. <br /><br /><i>This,</i> I feel, is the magic of Laini Taylor's writing. Or perhaps it's the magic of her plot. Either way, her stories unfold in such a realistic manner and best of all, she ensures that all this is palpable to the reader. Karou already made a niche in my heart in <i>Daughter of Smoke and Bone</i> but with <i>Days of Blood and Starlight</i> my heart wept for her. We see Karou at her most vulnerable and, at the same time, her most strong - mentally at least. It can't be said that Laini Taylor doesn't allow her character to grow, for she does. Each and every character we come across, from Akiva to Hazael and Liraz, his siblings, to Zuzanna and Mik, all experience <i>some</i> type of growth and change throughout this book. Akiva, especially, becomes a truly fleshed-out being, one whose personality is no longer as flat or connected to Karou's love as it once was. Now, seeing him as an individual with regrets, grief, and aspirations of his own, it is far easier to grow to truly love him as another person and not simply as Karou's lover. <br /><br />Furthermore, Laini Taylor simply outdoes herself with the world-building in this piece. Somehow, the battered, torn, and bloody land of Eratz has become such a real place in my mind that I wish to visit it and see it, for its simultaneous beauty and terror, all at once. Yet, for all its good qualities, I do have a <i>few</i> minor qualms with this novel, primarily, the set-up of the book itself. Unlike <i>Daughter of Smoke and Bone,</i> <i>Days of Blood and Starlight</i> flits between the perspectives of Karou, Akiva, Zuzanna, and a plethora of secondary characters we are unfamiliar with. While I enjoyed, for the most part, the round and full picture this type of storytelling provided us with, I also found that some small chapters could have been entirely done away with. I kept expecting them to play a greater role in the novel, and unfortunately, they didn't. In addition, the secondary (or quarterary?) characters we're introduced to have such little screen time that it's tough to feel anything much for them beyond fleeting thoughts. <br /><br />Nevertheless, that is a small qualm to have with a novel so perfect in every other way. <i>Days of Blood and Starlight</i> exceeded all my expectations (and mine were HIGH!) and surprised me with an uncanny amount of depth and a shocking slew of plot twists that had me simultaneously thrilled and upset. Furthermore, the amount of emotion this novel inspires is noteworthy. Taylor makes you feel for Karou and Akiva and while their romance, and their interactions for that matter, is <i>extremely</i> minimal, the bittersweet tone of their love is still felt. Neither Karou nor Akiva is at fault here and Taylor makes us see this so clearly in this piece that now, it is impossible to know in what direction the story will head. It ends off, much like <i>Daughter of Smoke and Bone</i> did, with a bittersweet kind of ending that leaves you aching for more, worried for these characters, and at the same time, filled with hope. I doubt I'd trust any other writer to take on such a complex novel - for truly Taylor has transformed a simple love story and made it into an intricate piece that leaves me with the knowledge that I still haven't understood it all, not <i>fully.</i> Needless to say, I cannot <i>wait</i> for the final installment in this trilogy. If there's anything I can count on, it's this: Laini Taylor will not disappoint. <br /><br />You can read <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com/2012/11/review-days-of-blood-and-starlight-by.html" rel="nofollow noopener">this review</a> and more on my blog, <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Ivy Book Bindings.</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="6289995636303671146" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_247319969" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/247319969" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/247319969?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=sci-fi-alicious">sci-fi-alicious</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=to-ya-or-not-to-ya">to-ya-or-not-to-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=ya-pnr-maddness">ya-pnr-maddness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=fun-fantasy">fun-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer247319969" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5689244529707171236">Days of Blood and Starlight was always going to be a hard sell after the stark and hauntingly beautiful Daughter of Smoke and Bone. I want to address the all-important question of whether Taylor has an obsession with the letters DBS or not.<br/><br/>Okay, fine. Not relevant. Really….party poopers.<br/><br/>Most of us had to prepare ourselves for the fact that DoBaS, like most middle child books, was probably not going to be quite as good as it’s older siblings. Personally, I always hold out hope for middle child bo</span>
  <span id="freeText5689244529707171236" style="display:none">Days of Blood and Starlight was always going to be a hard sell after the stark and hauntingly beautiful Daughter of Smoke and Bone. I want to address the all-important question of whether Taylor has an obsession with the letters DBS or not.<br /><br />Okay, fine. Not relevant. Really….party poopers.<br /><br />Most of us had to prepare ourselves for the fact that DoBaS, like most middle child books, was probably not going to be quite as good as it’s older siblings. Personally, I always hold out hope for middle child books, wanting to be pleasantly surprised!<br /><br />Well, the pessimistic, miserly old grinches win out this time because DoBaS isn’t quite as good as its predecessor, but it’s certainly nothing to turn your nose up at. But, you know, if you were to turn your nose up at any Laini Taylor book then, my god, have you no soul?!<br /><br />Taylor’s books have intense and varied themes. DoSaB’s themes revolved around perception, love and loss, the pain of emptiness and coming of age issues. DoBaS deals a lot with losing/regaining hope, faith in oneself, forgiveness of oneself and others.<br /><br />In a lot of ways DoBaS is a different creature to DoSaB. DoSaB had limited PoV changes that largely existed between Akiva and Karou (I think – my memory is really dodgy) and DoSaB was really more Romantic up until the very end. And by Romantic I don’t necessarily mean the relationship between Akiva and Karou because I ultimately think DoBaS was more romantic than its predecessor though it may not seem intuitively so. It was more Romantic in the sense that the characters and the story are so much bigger and more mature. There’s these two amazing, independent forces of fate building up behind Karou and Akiva. The more they come into themselves and become wiser, the more they’re drawn together.<br /><br />Daughter of Smoke and Bone is a naive, sweet innocent first love. Appealing to many, but I liked the relationship dynamics even more in Days of Blood and Starlight. They’ve both lost that naivette, grown as people. They have more baggage to deal with and the relationship they’re building feels stronger – erected on foundations off a deeper understanding of themselves and the world – and they still can’t help but love each other. After all they’ve seen, all they’ve done, all that’s been done to them – they’re still drawn to each other like moth’s to flame.<br /><br />Laini’s writing is beautiful. If anything she has improved and the inherent poetry to the writing has become sharper and more poignant. Where a lot of people, including myself will get tripped up at is that pacing and structure of the novel. It is very meandering with an excessive number of POV changes. There’s a lot to follow, a lot happening all at once and the cast of characters has expanded exponentially.<br /><br />But, over all, I loved it. I’m so enthusiastic for the next book. I absolutely have to know where this series is going, what’s going to happen to them and whether I’m just as naive and foolish as Akiva and Karou for hoping and thinking that they will eventually have some form of happy relationship at the end of this series.<br /><br />TAYLOR MARRY ME I LOVES YOU!<br /><br />This review also appears on my blog, <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com/blog/2012/11/27/arc-book-review-days-of-blood-and-starlight-by-laini-taylor/" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5689244529707171236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1957514273" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1957514273" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1957514273?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2017">z-read2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-high-fantasy">sff-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-series">x-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2017">z-faves2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2000">y-out2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1957514273" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12882172636511023188">I have to admit, I wasn't worried I wouldn't love this. I loved book one, after all! But this sequel is even better. In terms of character work and romantic arcs, I'm amazed at how far Laini Taylor has come. <br/><br/><b>HOW THIS BOOK LIVES UP TO BOOK ONE</b><br/><br/>• <b>The writing here is possibly even more beautiful</b>. Laini Taylor's writing flows across the page to the point where instead of skipping across paragraphs as I usually do, I was hanging on her every word. It's so simple and yet so gorgeous. I'd read her groce</span>
  <span id="freeText12882172636511023188" style="display:none">I have to admit, I wasn't worried I wouldn't love this. I loved book one, after all! But this sequel is even better. In terms of character work and romantic arcs, I'm amazed at how far Laini Taylor has come. <br /><br /><b>HOW THIS BOOK LIVES UP TO BOOK ONE</b><br /><br />• <b>The writing here is possibly even more beautiful</b>. Laini Taylor's writing flows across the page to the point where instead of skipping across paragraphs as I usually do, I was hanging on her every word. It's so simple and yet so gorgeous. I'd read her grocery lists. <br /><br />• This book is a complete <b>mindfuck</b>. Most of the twists towards the end are sheer brilliance. Taylor draws so many tiny threads into one beautiful big picture. This book makes it so you can guess all the twists, but you probably won't because they're never-before seen. <br /><br />• This isn't your typical angels vs. demons story; angels aren't all good and demons aren't all bad. I loved the <b>nuance</b> of their conflict. There's something to be said for taking an old story and making it something new, and I loved Laini Taylor's execution of this story. <br /><br /><b>HOW THIS SEQUEL IMPROVES ON BOOK ONE</b> <br /><br />The worldbuilding here is just awesome. It's even more complex than it was in book one, with a detailed world map and more complexity. <br /><br /><b>I am shocked at how many side characters I fell in love with here</b>. Karou's bravery and loneliness still shine brightly as ever. Her inner conflict over the Chimaera war stands out here; it's handled with nuance and grace. Liraz surprised me with her character development and nuance. Her brutality and desire to be more than a machine mix to form an extremely compelling character. Ziri's character surprised me as well; his conflict between ingrained prejudice and caring for others is very well-executed. Side characters like Hazael and Issa return, more fleshed out than ever, but possibly my favorite part was seeing <b>little flashes from chimaera and angels caught up in a war beyond their control</b>. Sarazal, Sveva, and Rath managed to touch my heart in the space of a few pages. <br /><br />Most changed award has to go to Akiva. He's changed so much since book one, where I liked but didn't love him. Here, he's an incredibly compelling character; <b>a character who's made huge mistakes and owns up to them.</b><br /><br />Improbable as their relationship is, <b>Karou and Akiva are such a compelling couple</b>. Their scenes here were few and far between, which served only to make them more tear-worthy. The touch of instalove from book one has become a complex relationship full of moments that touch your heart. They're seriously on the track towards becoming one of my top six couples. <br /><br />And of course, Zuzana and Mik are still delightful. I'm really glad Karou has girl friends and the book isn't a mess of slutshaming. These two also add <b>a touch of humor</b> to an otherwise disturbing story. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>“What is it about you?” she had asked him recently. “I almost never like people, even in tiny doses. But I never get tired of being with you.”<br />“It's my superpower,” he had said. “Extreme be-with-able-ness.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />This book is far darker, thematically, than DoSaB. <i>Days of Blood and Starlight</i> is a <b>war epic</b>, not just the story of a demon and angel's forbidden love. <b>Everything lovely about the first book is simply one part of a whole story.</b> There's so much <b>nuance</b> to both the themes and the characters; this is a book you could analyze for hours. <br /><br />Honestly, I think my feelings are best summed up my initial review being “I'm dead inside??” This book absolutely killed me, and I can't wait for book three. I know everyone has read this series already, but if you haven't, PLEASE pick it up. This is so much more than a cliche love story; it's about tragedy and war and prejudice and oh my god, please read it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12882172636511023188" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1843590542" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1843590542" />
    <a title="Ikram" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17065991-ikram"><img alt="Ikram" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505599855p2/17065991.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1843590542?book_show_action=true">Dec 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ikram" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ikram" href="/user/show/17065991-ikram">Ikram</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17065991-ikram?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17065991-ikram?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13074809051623330937"><blockquote>“A dream dirty and bruised is better than no dream at all.” </blockquote><br/><br/>After finishing <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/597744667' rel='nofollow noopener'>Daughter of Smoke & Bone.</a>, I immediately picked up the second book because this is one of those series you just can’t put down until you know every possible detail about it. For once, I’m really happy I didn’t start this series when it first came out because how can you possibly wait a whole year between each new release? This is what I like to call a marathonable series. <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483796418i/21649948.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/>The plot: <br/>This book took a turn for the bleak. I</span>
  <span id="freeText13074809051623330937" style="display:none"><blockquote>“A dream dirty and bruised is better than no dream at all.” </blockquote><br><br>After finishing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/597744667" rel="nofollow noopener">Daughter of Smoke &amp; Bone.</a>, I immediately picked up the second book because this is one of those series you just can’t put down until you know every possible detail about it. For once, I’m really happy I didn’t start this series when it first came out because how can you possibly wait a whole year between each new release? This is what I like to call a marathonable series. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483796418i/21649948.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>The plot: <br>This book took a turn for the bleak. It was definitely darker than the first one and that might be why I took one star off. I was hoping to see at least some uplifting scenes but for the most part this book focused on war, grief and revenge. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483796418i/21649949.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The romance: <br>*Sigh*I think it’s safe to say that my ship hit an iceberg in this book but I’m hoping things get fixed between Karou and Akiva in the final book. Kakiva needs to happen! <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483796418i/21649950.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> The characters: <br>➨Ziri: Ziri was surprisingly my favorite character in this book. The poor guy has the biggest crush on Karou and has been in the friendzone since he was a kid. <br><br>Also, can we just talk about his body for a sec? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[We made such a big deal about him being the last chimera with his original body to then sacrifice it and put him in the wolf! Why! Just why! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>➨Zuzana: I’m still confused about the magic system in this world. How does it work? How come a human can learn to disappear? I need answers.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483796418i/21649951.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>➨Thiago: I knew right off the bat that we couldn’t trust that f*cking asshole. I get it, Karou had no choice but to work with him but ughh <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I wish she would have killed him sooner. That rape scene destroyed my heart.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I’m really not sure how I feel about <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Ziri being in the wolf’s body. I just hope we can somehow get him back to his own body at some point.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>➨Jael: Somebody needs to kill this thing before I do. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483796418i/21649952.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>What I’m hoping to see in the next book: <br>➨ Kakiva sailing. <br>➨Festival: Akiva’s mother. I hope we can learn more about her story and how she <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[destroyed Jael’s face.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>➨More explanation on the magic system. <br>➨<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Get Ziri back to his own body for God’s sake.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>➨ Brimstone back? Maybe? Hopefully? <br><br>Thanks for reading! Please share your thoughts :D <br><br><br><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_852488164" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/852488164" />
    <a title="Regan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19645927-regan"><img alt="Regan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437809914p2/19645927.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/852488164?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Regan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Regan" href="/user/show/19645927-regan">Regan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19645927-regan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19645927-regan?shelf=books-owned-read">books-owned-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer852488164" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer609407503678058556">This book was amazing. I enjoyed the first book, but this one was leagues ahead. <br/><br/>The one thing I really appreciated about this story was the tone. I felt that Laini Taylor expertly captured the feeling of war. Taylor painted both sides as exhausted and frustrated, the soldiers were unable to articulate why they were fighting anymore. All they knew was blood. There was this air of hopelessness, this feeling that neither side was winning, that both were destroying themselves. But even within this </span>
  <span id="freeText609407503678058556" style="display:none">This book was amazing. I enjoyed the first book, but this one was leagues ahead. <br /><br />The one thing I really appreciated about this story was the tone. I felt that Laini Taylor expertly captured the feeling of war. Taylor painted both sides as exhausted and frustrated, the soldiers were unable to articulate why they were fighting anymore. All they knew was blood. There was this air of hopelessness, this feeling that neither side was winning, that both were destroying themselves. But even within this desolate landscape Taylor also sprinkled in small flames of hope to keep us going. <br /><br />This book was wonderfully written, and I cannot wait for the final book in the series coming out in April. Highly recommended. </span>

<div id="review_270555282" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/270555282" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/270555282?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Stacia (the 2010 club) by: </span>
      buddy read with sandra, jenny and meg
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=angels-nephilim-and-demons">angels-nephilim-and-demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=general-fantasy-and-mythology">general-fantasy-and-mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=hybrid-multiple-genre">hybrid-multiple-genre</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=beautiful-word-porn">beautiful-word-porn</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer270555282" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15781342793548767962"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>These are the Days of Blood & Starlight.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368732i/721315.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Oh, Ellai, my hands will never be clean again.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><b>4.5 stars</b>. I want to crawl inside of Laini Taylor's head and live there for a little while. For every creative idea I've ever had, it feels like a penny compared to a hundred dollar bill. Laini falls on the idea-rich side.<br/><br/>In the past, you might have seen my enthusiastic gushing about book 1 and how I likened it to <i>word porn</i>. Because, you know, that's what it was - porn for the brain that</span>
  <span id="freeText15781342793548767962" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>These are the Days of Blood &amp; Starlight.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368732i/721315.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Oh, Ellai, my hands will never be clean again.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>4.5 stars</b>. I want to crawl inside of Laini Taylor's head and live there for a little while. For every creative idea I've ever had, it feels like a penny compared to a hundred dollar bill. Laini falls on the idea-rich side.<br><br>In the past, you might have seen my enthusiastic gushing about book 1 and how I likened it to <i>word porn</i>. Because, you know, that's what it was - porn for the brain that wants to live in a realm of lush visuals and beautiful prose. <br><br>Book 2 was no different, yet it somehow was. I completely understand why so many people love book 2 even better than the first, but I'm going to come clean here : <i>I struggled to get through the first half</i>. The PoV's were jumping all over the place, the scenery was going back and forth, and I really just wanted to see a certain two individuals come face-to-face again.<br><br><b>But then I hit the 50% mark. And it was like brain orgasms all over the place.</b> Because, you know, (yes...I'm wearing this phrase out) - MOTHEREFFING WORD PORN. <br><br>All of a sudden, I could see the pretty colors. All of a sudden, my chest started aching with longing for certain things to happen. All of sudden, I wanted to retrieve every single thing which had been lost. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I lost my soul. I lost our dream. Vengeance eclipsed everything.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>How does this woman/author/creative goddess do it? I want to bottle her secret. I want to see each and every single chimera and angel in my head but can't wrap my mind around it. I need to have these visuals brought to the big screen because my tiny little brain can't fathom how awesome all of these creatures must look.<br><br>And Karou...Akiva...the emotions...all over the place, just as my jumbled review thoughts must be. How do I explain the large scope of issues that are Karou and Akiva? How can I even begin to explain the feels these two put me through? And Ziri - oh how I wanted to hug Ziri.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Her name means hope. But not in their language, and not for them.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>If you haven't started this series yet and desire to want to live in a place where fantasy meets reality, in a moment of time when two worlds collide, get ready for something like you haven't seen before and might never see again.<br><br>BUT...don't do what I did and read books 1 and 2 so far apart. I think I might have given this book 5 stars if I'd read it right after book 1. It's a shame that I struggled so much to get my love back. I knew it would happen, but it took much longer the second time around. <br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15781342793548767962" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer77520563471932192"><i> "And on Akiva's face, gratitude vied with the emptiness that Liraz had started thinking of as his death wish look. She remembered a time when Akiva had laughed and smiled, when in spite of the violence of their lives he had been a full person, with a full range of emotion. He had never had Hazael's sunshine demeanour - who did? But he had been alive. Once upon a time." </i><br/><br/>A fantastic continuation of the Daughter of Smoke and Bone trilogy.   <span id="freeText77520563471932192" style="display:none"><i> "And on Akiva's face, gratitude vied with the emptiness that Liraz had started thinking of as his death wish look. She remembered a time when Akiva had laughed and smiled, when in spite of the violence of their lives he had been a full person, with a full range of emotion. He had never had Hazael's sunshine demeanour - who did? But he had been alive. Once upon a time." </i><br /><br />A fantastic continuation of the Daughter of Smoke and Bone trilogy. I loved being back in the world of Seraphim and Chimera. <br /><br />SPOILERS AHEAD!!!!<br /><br />Karou is left reeling from the revelation of what happened to Brimstone and the rest of her family, after regaining her memory and learning about her past as Madgrial. She returns to Eretz to live with the other Chimera and carry on Brimstone's work, while under the thumb of Thiago - the white wolf. Whom I hate with the fire of a thousand suns just FYI.<br /><br />Meanwhile Akiva is back with his brother and sister, fighting in the war, nothing but weapons in this never ending fight. The leader of the Seraphim has some terrible plans, and Akiva wants to do whatever he can to stop them.<br /><br />We get more of Zuzanna and Mik! I love these two :) I love how Laini managed to incorporate them into the fantastical world of Angels and Monsters. Plus the ending of book 2 sets us up to dive straight back into the action, so I need book 3 now!</span>

<div id="review_272053359" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/272053359" />
    <a title="Kristalia " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5705623-kristalia"><img alt="Kristalia " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535637983p2/5705623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/272053359?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristalia " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristalia " href="/user/show/5705623-kristalia">Kristalia </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone who like mature ya and combination of contemporary and high fantasy :D</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=own-physical-copy">own-physical-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=be-my-heroes-please">be-my-heroes-please</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=they-are-so-awesome-hot-and-stuff">they-are-so-awesome-hot-and-stuff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=unique-or-different-story">unique-or-different-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=favorites-absolute">favorites-absolute</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=masterpiece">masterpiece</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=favorite-couple">favorite-couple</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer272053359" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8185093185216947574"><b>Final rating: 5/5 stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411366823i/11218831._SY540_.png' width='400' alt='note: silkette is my irl friend and she gave me permission to use her photos for making this ♥' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
<i> <b>“Once upon a time, an angel and a devil fell in love and dared to imagine a new way of living—one without massacres and torn throats and bonfires of the fallen, without revenants or bastard armies or children ripped from their mothers’ arms to take their turn in the killing and dying.<br/><br/>Once, the lovers lay entwined in the moon’s secret temple and dreamed of a world that was a like a jewel-box without a jewel—a paradise waiting for them to find it and fill it with their hap</b></i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText8185093185216947574" style="display:none"><b>Final rating: 5/5 stars</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411366823i/11218831._SY540_.png" width="400" alt="note: silkette is my irl friend and she gave me permission to use her photos for making this ♥" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
<i> <b>“Once upon a time, an angel and a devil fell in love and dared to imagine a new way of living—one without massacres and torn throats and bonfires of the fallen, without revenants or bastard armies or children ripped from their mothers’ arms to take their turn in the killing and dying.<br><br>Once, the lovers lay entwined in the moon’s secret temple and dreamed of a world that was a like a jewel-box without a jewel—a paradise waiting for them to find it and fill it with their happiness.This was not that world.”</b></i> </blockquote><br><br><br><b> When you read a trilogy, does it make you feel that the second one is always a bridge between books? Where nothing of importance happens in it?<br><br>What if i say that this book was NOT a bridge, but carefully and well done story where each and every character is important? Where the story was so great that it felt epic? <br><br>Well, this is what Days of Blood &amp; Starlight is. Total and utter EPICNESS.<br><br><br><u>*this review holds spoilers for Daughter of Smoke and Bone... you have been warned*</u></b><br><br>● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● <br><br>I adored that<b>
  <i> this was not dedicated to love story between Akiva and Karou.</i>
</b> Actually, it's all about <b>
  <i> war in Eretz</i>
</b> and what happens to the world, not them. Which was <b>
  <i> fantastic</i>
</b>. <br><br>Don't be confused... it is still a love story, but it's in the background. And after that shock plot twist from the first book, i totally understand Karou AND Akiva. What i really love are the characters, new and old ones, their complexity and deepness. We are introduced to new characters such as Ziri, Rath,Sarazal and Sveva, and also reunited with the old character such as Mik and Zuzana, Hazael and Liraz and of course <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ issa ♥  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> who are all fantastically characterized.<br><br>Anyway....it was <b>
  <i>gorgeous,</i>
</b> such awesomely made world building !<b>
  <i> I love how the book was dedicated to explaining Eretz, Seraphim hierarchy, also from Chimaera's point of view.</i>
</b> It was amazing!!!<br><br><br><br>● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● <br><br><blockquote>
<i> <b>Once upon a time, an angel and a devil held a wishbone between them.<br><br>And its snap split the world in two.</b></i> </blockquote><br><br>After the shocking turn of the events, Karou is living in a "Sandcastle" in the middle of the desert on Earth, where it has the portal to Eretz. She finally found out who she is and was, and is trying to make things right again, by making a new army of chimaera. <br><br>While Akiva tries to redeem himself in Eretz, by trying to help as much as he can, for both races.... <br><br>And both Seraphim and Chimaera start a war which can't be stopped - while darkness and corruption creeps to destroy everything around them. <br><br><br>There is a little of happening in human world, 95% of the book happens in Eretz :D<br><br><br>___________________________________________<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>Characters</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br>____________________________________________<br><br>*these might be a little spoilerish, but nothing that will spoil the story too much. Can't say the same for spoiler tags. They are quite serious*<br><br>♦ <b>
  <u> Karou </u>
</b>:<br><br><br> <blockquote>
<i> <b> “I am one of billions. I am stardust gathered fleetingly into form. I will be ungathered. The stardust will go on to be other things someday and I will be free.” </b></i> </blockquote><br><br>Karou tried to help chimaeras, she only wanted peace, but it was hard with slaughtering of chimaera, their enslavement and their war with Seraphim. She tried to make things right, she wanted to tell everyone that she was not traitor, that she never betrayed their secrets <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(cause it was Thiago, telling everything to Akiva when he tortured him, of course)....  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br><br>Karou and Akiva had something unique, something wonderful, and it all ended because Akiva destroyed it all - because he wanted to avenge Madrigal. <br><br> <blockquote>
<i> <b> "Let's see. You know how, at the end of Romeo and Juliet, Juliet wakes up in the crypt and Romeo's already dead? He thought she was dead so he killed himself right next to her?"<br>"Yeah. That was awesome." A pause, followed by "Ow," suggested elbow punctuation on the part of Mik.<br>Karou ignored it. "Well, imagine if she woke up and he was still alive, but..." She swallowed, waiting out a tremor in her voice. "But he had killed her whole family. And burned her city. And killed and enslaved her people.” </b></i> </blockquote><br><br>He did it for her, because he was out of his mind, watching his love being murdered in front of his eyes. He lived for revenge - and all because he thought she was dead (not that i approve of what he had done). <br><br>Karou was fantastic. She didn't irritate me, i love her, i approve of her decisions, expect for one. Her ignoring Akiva. His love for her is so strong, and she doesn't understand it. She tried to change their love to lust, and she knew it was not possible.<br><br><b>So...coming to an end, i must spoil a lot so.... </b><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I am glad that she was resurectionist, and even though she was never thanked for it, she ensured the survival of her race. On the other hand, Thiago was such a bastard, especially when he tried to rape her. I am so glad she got to kill him before he did anything. Alas, it happened at the end of the book -.-  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>♦ <b>
  <u> Akiva </u>
</b>: <br><br><br> <blockquote>
<i> <b> “What can a soldier do when mercy is treason, and he is alone in it?” </b></i> </blockquote><br><br>*minor spoilers*<br><br>Akiva was in terrible situation, he made so much mistakes (some of them really pissed me off), but he did it because he truly loved Karou/Madrigal, and he was spying on her, trying to keep her safe, always been there for her. He did everything to redeem himself, he never wanted for any of this to happen. I am just sad that every time they spoke, it ended with her hurting him. Always. He goes to her and leaves broken in pieces.<br><br>Other than that, i always knew he wouldn't be the type to hunt and kill chimaera, even if they are enemies. Even after all he went through because of them, he wanted peace as well. He, Liraz and Hazael were unstoppable trio, capable of anything, always doing the right thing. They both have forgiven him, and helped them every way they could. I am glad i learned more about him, and his thinking. <br><br><b> Must spoil a lot now, beware - major spoilers </b><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <br>I am so glad he did what he should have, i had a feeling it would happen but still, i am glad he killed Joram. Even though he was his father, Joram was terrorist, worst type of tyrant and i am glad he met his end with Akiva's sword through his heart. <br><br>His mother's mystery is so-so revealed. Her name is Festival, she was killed by Jael, when she gave him the scare upon his face, and so...that story ends. <br><br>I was sad that Akiva is such a tragic soul....Really....He went through so much just to earn Karou's trust again. He saved Ziri from certain doom, he saved all he could and it still wasn't enough. <br><br>And, he is magi, he summoned birds, can be invisible, can put things and people invisible, can cause whatever he caused at the end of the book.<br><br>Also the part where he comes to Karou with Liraz and Hazael was so heartbreaking, especially when he was thinking that she had betrayed their love with Thiago, his torturer and her killer, and even fainted because he couldn't do anything, he was powerless and tired from all of it, in shock, and in the end, he just wished he would never wake up again. How can i not love Akiva? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>♦ <b>
  <u> Hazael and Liraz </u>
</b>: <br><br><br> <blockquote>
<i> <b><br>“As long as you're alive, there's always a chance things will get better."<br>"Or worse," said Liraz.<br>"Yes," he conceded. "Usually worse."<br>Hazael cut in. "My sister, Sunshine, and my brother, Light. You two should rally the ranks. You'll have us killing ourselves by morning.” </b></i> </blockquote><br><br> Hazael and Liraz were so awesome. I am glad they appeared so much more than in DOSAB. It was so awesome having chapters with them: Hazael's humor and Liraz's awesomeness. Those two were the epic duo, and with Akiva they did everything they wanted. They are siblings and they love each other so much, that they are ready to forgive anything of the other one.<br><br><b> Major spoiler concerning the two: </b> <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I was so sad when Haz died....Especially impaled on the sword when Emperor was killed. I was so stricken by the devastation of Akiva and Liraz....They were in such a shock that they had to turn to Chimaera for help.....It wasn't pretty to see Liraz lose it that much, and even Akiva........  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>♦ <b>
  <u> Ziri</u>
</b>: <br><br><br><br>i freaking love him!!! Last of the Kirin race, he was such pure awesomeness. I loved every chapter with him. Elegant, cute and totally i-want-to-squeeze-you-right-now type. I didn't approve of his ignoring of Karou in the begining, but he had a reason&gt;after all, fear rules common reason. But still, he was Karou's hope, he was the last one that was from her Clan.... Anyway, i simply adored him ♥<br><br><b> Major spoiler concerning the end and middle</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I was so sad when they captured him and tortured him.. Thankfully, Akiva saved him from being violated even more (like he didn't have his arms destroyed and his face carved with a Jocker type of smile....Poor guy). <br><br>i also liked that he loves Karou, but not in love triangle style, but in idol style. He stalked her (ok, that was wrong). But he knew that he would never be hers. He knew that what Akiva and Karou had was absolutely wonderful, and he was one of the rare ones who was sad when they did Madrigal's execution. He felt for Akiva, he understood his pain, he understood him in general, and Akiva in return, unconsciously returned that favor by saving him. <br><br>I was also shocked when he slitted his throat to be resurrected as Thiago, his worst enemy. He did it for Karou, but he also did it to stop this useless war.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>♦ <b>
  <u> Mik and Zuzana </u>
</b>: <br><br>ah they are so so so much cute ♥3♥ I don't know who to love more. I like Zuzana's craziness and their love and i just love them in general, and that they are true friends. They were always there to help. Some spoilers, nothing major <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I love how they searched for Karou, how they didn't quit searching, how they found her, helped her, were always there for her.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><br><br>♦ <b>
  <u> Thiago,Joram and Jael </u>
</b>: <br><br>Thiago is such a tyrant, terrorist, and everything evil. I just hate him with passion. I actually don't know who to hate more of the trio (joram, jael or thiago XD) Anyway, i didn't approve of his methods, especially of slaughtering angels and doing it all because of revenge, not because of survival. <br><br>As for Seraphim ones, i don't know which one is worse. Joram,the emperor &amp; the tyrant who makes a lot of bastards called Misbegotten, who are almost war slaves to Seraphim or Jael,emperor's brother, who has an army called Dominion, but everyone who is in it must sometimes be in his bed. Ugh, disgusting. No wonder why the war is raging =.= <br><br>And so,the true goal of Joram and Jael is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ go through the portals into human world where they would be worshiped as gods, take their weapons and doom chimaera. In which they succeded.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>♦ <b>
  <u> Rath,Sarazal and Sveva </u>
</b>: <br><br>I found this story very interesting. Because of war, Rath from the Dashnag clan, which is famous for being cannibals of their own race and Sarazal &amp; Sveva, two dama's who are usually the main food to Dashnag-started to defend each other, and united despite their differences. Rath saved them both, kept them safe. I am glad that we got their story too, their perspective. It just proved one point - no matter how different they are, in this war, they are all united.<br><br>____________________________________________<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>OVERALL</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br>____________________________________________<br><br><br><br><b>This book is a worthy sequel, fast page turner, short chapters, awesome characters, little of love story, even better world building than Daughter of smoke and bone, intriguing, fast paced, cliff hanger chapters, and war, enslavement, terror, slaughter, betrayals, submission, and love. I want to read this over and over again!!! (Please, please please, let the movie be awesome and have second one too!!!) </b><br><br>____________________________________________<br><br>● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ●<br>____________________________________________ <br><br><b> MY DAUGHTER OF SMOKE AND BONE REVIEWS: </b><br><br>◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/272053338" rel="nofollow noopener"> Daughter of Smoke &amp; Bone (Daughter of Smoke &amp; Bone #1) </a><br>◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/272053359" rel="nofollow noopener"> Days of Blood &amp; Starlight (Daughter of Smoke and Bone, #2) </a><br>◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/334082097" rel="nofollow noopener"> Dreams of Gods &amp; Monsters (Daughter of Smoke and Bone, #3) </a><br><br><br><b>

<div id="review_446830265" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/446830265" />
    <a title="TheBookSmugglers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1223249-thebooksmugglers"><img alt="TheBookSmugglers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316717753p2/1223249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/446830265?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TheBookSmugglers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TheBookSmugglers" href="/user/show/1223249-thebooksmugglers">TheBookSmugglers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1223249-thebooksmugglers?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1223249-thebooksmugglers?shelf=romantic-fantasy">romantic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer446830265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12891601731298989264">Original review posted on <a href='http://thebooksmugglers.com/2012/11/book-review-days-of-blood-and-starlight-by-laini-taylor.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Book Smugglers</a><br/><br/><i>Warning: this review contains inevitable spoilers for book 1 in the series. <br/>Trigger warning: rape.</i><br/><br/>Laini Taylor is doing really interesting things with her series. When it comes to romance in the Paranormal/Fantasy YA landscape, more often than not the reader is presented with truly problematic pairings where rape culture is normalised and where insta-love is presented as par for de course and in lieu of actual romantic development.<br/><br/>Daughter of Smoke and</span>
  <span id="freeText12891601731298989264" style="display:none">Original review posted on <a href="http://thebooksmugglers.com/2012/11/book-review-days-of-blood-and-starlight-by-laini-taylor.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book Smugglers</a><br /><br /><i>Warning: this review contains inevitable spoilers for book 1 in the series. <br />Trigger warning: rape.</i><br /><br />Laini Taylor is doing really interesting things with her series. When it comes to romance in the Paranormal/Fantasy YA landscape, more often than not the reader is presented with truly problematic pairings where rape culture is normalised and where insta-love is presented as par for de course and in lieu of actual romantic development.<br /><br />Daughter of Smoke and Bone was a book with a very strong focus in the romance between Karou/Madrigal and Akiva. A romance that was not only forged on the insta-love Furnace of Doom but also one depicted as having the no holds barred/soul mates kind of dynamic. That love was all the more impacting because it was also an impossible romance between enemies who dared to dream about ending the war between their people. At the end of that book, we know how well this turned out (not): Madrigal was killed but eventually resurrected as memory-less Karou. Akiva, thinking Madrigal was well and truly dead, went on a killing rampage. It ended with Karou recovering her memories and realising what Akiva had done and the two breaking up, therefore subverting the usual YA romantic trope and that was AWESOME.<br /><br />At one point in Days of Blood and Starlight, Karou says that their story is like Romeo and Juliet’s but instead of waking up to find that Romeo had committed suicide, she wakes up to find out that he went on to decimate not only her entire immediate family, destroy her city and then proceed to commit genocide against her entire race. Lovely.<br /><br />And that’s the actual starting point here: the insta-love that doesn’t work and is not rewarded for its wtfuckery. The story then in Days of Blood and Starlight deals with the after, with the guilt, with Karou finding out that HOLY CRAP, she dared to dream of love and that’s what happens when you hook up with a fanatical dude. Because there is no denying: Akiva has lost his shit so completely and how do you come back from that?<br /><br />You can’t. Because genocide: not an acceptable response to your lover’s death.<br /><br />Akiva knows that. Karou knows that. And so they are apart. And in the “apart”, they come to realise that their dream of peace needs to be bigger than their dream of togetherness.<br /><br />But enough with the romance because unlike what I might have led you to believe with my rambling above, this book is not about love at all, it is actually about war. Karou is back with the few surviving Chimera, working alongside Thiago, the abhorrent man who killed her, in order to create an army of monsters to avenge their people.<br /><br />In the meantime, there is a lot of emotional angst here. Karou is drowning in guilt for daring to fall in love with the enemy and mistakenly equates her dream of peace and love with the ensuing mass-murders on both sides. Part of her journey is realising that the love and the dream are not the problem. Revenge is. But before she gets to this realisation, the Karou of the first book is replaced with a meek, emo-version of herself, someone who makes terrible, stupid mistakes in the name of making amends (at one point I actually expected Akiva and Karou to burst into singing “I had a dream my life would be so different from this hell I am living”).<br /><br />And it’s like, being complicit with genocide: not an acceptable response to your guilt.<br /><br />Sorry, going back to the romance briefly: I do wonder what is going to happen. Because surely there is no way to mend this. NO WAY. There can’t be. Especially considering that yes, Akiva feels immense guilt, but his guilt comes only once he knows Karou is alive. If she was still dead, I got the feeling he would not feel this way. And I have a sneaky suspicion that because both of them have been involved with mass killings to some extent or another, in some creepy way all could be forgiven in the end because both did unspeakable things? Like in a really wonky, problematic mathematical equation in which each other’s actions are annulled like they never happened or something because… True Love. Surely, this is not where this story is going, is it?<br /><br />And I can’t begin to express how fucked up this is, and how terrible the consequences are. And it becomes really clear, really soon, how their world is the shittiest place EVER. Both Angels and Chimera are immersed in this bloody war and holy crap, this book is dark, violent and emotionally draining and at points I just wanted to stop reading and get out just so I could breathe. In fact, reading some pages felt like being punched.<br /><br />Laini Taylor is a brilliant writer and there is no denying that the harrowing version of Karou’s story is as engaging and beautifully written as its lighter companion (book one).<br /><br />Those things said, I can’t help but to think that structurally speaking this book is a bit of a mess. There is a lot of head-hopping with random characters providing the point of view for a couple of pages then disappearing altogether from the narrative.<br /><br />There is also a point toward the ending of the book where the narrative – which thus far had been linear – becomes choppy as it goes back to hours or days before a certain point in the present time just so there could be an extremely contrived “gotcha” moment.<br /><br />Zuzana and her boyfriend Mik, as awesome as they are – and I mean it, I just love their love story as well as the loyalty and friendship between Karou and Zuzana – had no place in this story. Although I get the intention of adding a lighter tone to an otherwise grim story as well as giving Karou some footing in the human world, their presence in the proceedings felt forced and their comic lightness was misplaced in the midst of such portentous happenings.<br /><br />Finally, part of me wonders if some of this violence isn’t a bit gratuitous, just to make a point. And then you have an extremely violent and completely unnecessary attempted rape scene. As though there wasn’t enough evidence of the violent and abhorrent nature of the attacker already so let’s add humiliating sexual violence toward its main female character as well.<br /><br />Ultimately, Days of Blood and Starlight is an emotionally impacting book with a solid story and good overall plot developments. But unfortunately, it is nowhere near as awesome as its predecessor.<br /><br />But, as I said before: Laini Taylor is doing really interesting things with her series. I just don’t know how I feel about them. I do remain curious to see where it goes though. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12891601731298989264" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2765251483" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2765251483" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2765251483?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2019-shelf">2019-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2765251483" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3162126652470899986">Dark.<br/><br/>Deliciously dark. Where the first book had the whole star-crossed romance going on, we are DONE with that. Well, almost. The weight of betrayal and hopelessness kinda did that in. And now we've got an ongoing and endless war ahead of us. <br/><br/>Am I impressed that the tale turned on such a dime without feeling at all forced? Yep. Absolutely. And I'm even more impressed that no one at all seems to be worth saving. <br/><br/>But there's hope. Oh, yes, there's still hope. And love. Even if it is mostly squashe</span>
  <span id="freeText3162126652470899986" style="display:none">Dark.<br /><br />Deliciously dark. Where the first book had the whole star-crossed romance going on, we are DONE with that. Well, almost. The weight of betrayal and hopelessness kinda did that in. And now we've got an ongoing and endless war ahead of us. <br /><br />Am I impressed that the tale turned on such a dime without feeling at all forced? Yep. Absolutely. And I'm even more impressed that no one at all seems to be worth saving. <br /><br />But there's hope. Oh, yes, there's still hope. And love. Even if it is mostly squashed to hell, the love and magic still have a chance.<br /><br />Do I have some sort of goofy grin on my face? Possibly. Maybe. You'd think I'd have gotten my fill of this kind of thing by now since everyone and their little fat dogs have got a hand in this same game. The YA market seems to be nothing but this kind of thing.<br /><br />BUT. Quality will rise to the top and this is quality. So no more complaining, ya'll.<br /><br />I can't wait to see what comes next.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3162126652470899986" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2765251483">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2237965829" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12422730286427842778"><b>this was amazing!</b> I enjoyed it so much more then book one. I CANNOT RECOMMEND THE AUDIOBOOK ENOUGH THE NARRATION IS BEAUTIFUL AND CAPTIVATING <br/><br/>Okay, I enjoyed this so much more then book one because it focussed much more on the war and the political going ons within the Angel and Chimera communities. So many things explored were so interesting, especially resurrection and I LOVED ALL THE PLOT TWISTS AND HOW LAINI TAYLOR SETS YOU UP FOR AN EXPECTATION THE UNDERCUTS YOU<br/><br/>Also, I literally love the ch</span>
  <span id="freeText12422730286427842778" style="display:none"><b>this was amazing!</b> I enjoyed it so much more then book one. I CANNOT RECOMMEND THE AUDIOBOOK ENOUGH THE NARRATION IS BEAUTIFUL AND CAPTIVATING <br /><br />Okay, I enjoyed this so much more then book one because it focussed much more on the war and the political going ons within the Angel and Chimera communities. So many things explored were so interesting, especially resurrection and I LOVED ALL THE PLOT TWISTS AND HOW LAINI TAYLOR SETS YOU UP FOR AN EXPECTATION THE UNDERCUTS YOU<br /><br />Also, I literally love the characters so much. Karou, Zuzannah, Mik and Akiva, Xirri and Haziel and Loraz (cannot tell you if those are spelt right due to audio lmao) ARE ALL SO GOOD I love them! Every character is so well fleshed out and dynamic it makes it so interesting<br /><br />Anyway I am so glad I enjoyed this so much I cannot wait to listen to Dreams of Gods and Monsters full review to come</span>

<div id="review_2823049702" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2823049702" />
    <a title="Lucy Langford" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74034800-lucy-langford"><img alt="Lucy Langford" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518091381p2/74034800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2823049702?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy Langford" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy Langford" href="/user/show/74034800-lucy-langford">Lucy Langford</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444722703" href="/book/show/18048665-days-of-blood-starlight">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2823049702" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14382599021795912466">I liked this book better than the first one. This book takes off from the first one and Karou is the new resurrectionist for the Chimera army.<br/><br/>I liked this one as it explained more about the history between the Seraphim and the Chimera. There was much more action as well and tensions between the “creatures” and characters personally, made for an interesting set up. <br/><br/>Of course Zuzanna was there again to provide some comedic relief and also support for Karou. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('81JyeXHyUAlBiuDcDXZPfOtll08TI+M+zKXiWjCyJVfJdBuryqyZYeahVL36g0WjPTpwh92ubVmX26Tr/fHXzQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KUZnb73/A6WcxJtUfZMCqHWE8plkjSFm6i5COaT7Fa0TYA69BqHKzTvvLzWKZgh3o9sVUaoArwGxUASIabjnNw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText17893711538305198180" style="display:none">Hi! I write fantasy books. My latest is STRANGE THE DREAMER, about a young librarian, a mythic lost city, and the half-human children of murdered gods. Check it out :-) Before that I wrote the DAUGHTER OF SMOKE &amp; BONE trilogy, which has been translated into 32 languages. It's about a blue-haired art student raised by monsters, a broken angel, and a war that has raged for 1000 years in another world. I also wrote LIPS TOUCH: THREE TIMES, which was a National Book Award finalist, and the DREAMDARK books. As well as various short stories and novellas. <br /><br />Thanks for reading!! <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.lainitaylor.com">www.lainitaylor.com</a><br /><br />@lainitaylor</span>
